---
  description: Define the grouping structure by mapping group to a variable that has a different value for each group and then convert them with ggplotly
  function: aes_group_order
  permalink: /ggplot2/aesthetics/aes_group_order/
  layout: base
  language: ggplot2
  name: aes_group_order
  reference: https://ggplot2.tidyverse.org/reference/
---


# Default scatterplot


<pre class="mcode">
p <- ggplot(mtcars, aes(wt, mpg))
p <-  p + geom_point(size = 4)

plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

# Using colour


<pre class="mcode">
p <- ggplot(mtcars, aes(wt, mpg))
p <-  p + geom_point(aes(colour = factor(cyl)), size = 4)

plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

# Using shape


<pre class="mcode">
p <- ggplot(mtcars, aes(wt, mpg))
p <-  p + geom_point(aes(shape = factor(cyl)), size = 4)

plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

# Using fill

Default plot:


<pre class="mcode">
p <- ggplot(mtcars, aes(factor(cyl)))
p <-  p + geom_bar()

plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

# Multiple groups with one aesthetic

The default is not sufficient here. A single line tries to connect all the observations.

<pre class="mcode">
p <- ggplot(nlme::Oxboys, aes(age, height))
p <-  p + geom_line()

plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

To fix this, use the group aesthetic to map a different line for each subject.


<pre class="mcode">
p <- ggplot(nlme::Oxboys, aes(age, height))
p <-  p + geom_line(aes(group = Subject))

plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

# Different groups on different layers

Using the group aesthetic with both `geom_line()` and `geom_smooth()` groups the data the same way for both layers


<pre class="mcode">
p <- p + geom_line(aes(group = Subject))
p <-  p + geom_smooth(aes(group = Subject), method = "lm", se = FALSE)

plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

Changing the group aesthetic for the smoother layer fits a single line of best fit across all.

<pre class="mcode">
p <- p + geom_line(aes(group = Subject))
p <-  p + geom_smooth(aes(group = 1), size = 2, method = "lm", se = FALSE)

plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

# Overriding the default grouping

Sometimes the plot has a discrete scale but you want to draw lines that connect across groups. This is the strategy used in interaction plots, profile plots, and parallel coordinate plots, among others.

For example, draw boxplots of height at each measurement occasion:

<pre class="mcode">
p <- ggplot(nlme::Oxboys, aes(Occasion, height)) + geom_boxplot()

plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

    ssim="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/plotly/ssim_baselines/main/out_ggplot2/ggplot2/Aesthetics/aes_group_order/example12_ssim_map.png"

There is no need to specify the group aesthetic here; the default grouping works because occasion is a discrete variable. To overlay individual trajectories, we again need to override the default grouping for that layer with `aes(group = Subject)`



<pre class="mcode">
p <- ggplot(nlme::Oxboys, aes(Occasion, height)) + geom_boxplot()
p <-  p + geom_line(aes(group = Subject), colour = "blue")

plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>
